## Open decisions / parked

> Things deliberately not decided yet. Don't silently resolve these тАФ flag them.

- **The 8-step onboarding wizard was sunset** (cleanup pass). Client creation is now the `CreateClientModal` quick-create flow (see the `admin/` create-client inventory section). The wizard routes, `lib/onboarding/`, `components/admin/onboarding/`, `WizardSectionEditor`, the wizard-only `AutomationCard`, and `BuilderLayout` / `PreviewPanelBar` were deleted. `builder-design.md ┬з5` and `builder-generation-design.md ┬з3` carry SUPERSEDED banners.
- **Lead-capture forms** тАФ the form builder (the `editForms` capability, the `form` section type, the `Section.form` envelope config, `form_submitted` lead events) shipped after Cluster 9; the retroactive design doc is `reference/form-builder-design.md`. Files: `lib/website/form-config.ts`, `lib/website/sections/form.tsx`, `components/shared/website/{FormBlock,FormFieldTypePicker,SectionFormControls}.tsx`. Public-site rendering of forms is the remaining piece, deferred with the public-render pipeline.
- **Auth тАФ DONE (real Supabase Auth, end to end).** `backend-schema-design.md ┬з6` / `[JC-10]` called for real Supabase Auth; it is wired (`7ceda3c` Phase 2, `b07a79c` Phase 3 fix, `341d19f` Phase 5). `user-stub.tsx` (misnamed тАФ kept for import stability) resolves the signed-in user from a real `supabase.auth` session; `(auth)/login` is a real `signInWithPassword` screen; `capability_grants` are live rows; `DataHydrationProvider` hydrates the in-memory stores from Supabase on every auth change. **A logged-out page load shows a wall of `401 permission denied` console warnings** тАФ `DataHydrationProvider` fires `hydrateAll()` on mount before a session exists and the `anon` role is correctly refused; it re-hydrates after sign-in. That is expected noise, not a bug. **Still owed:** a deliberate cross-tenant RLS validation pass тАФ the policies have not been systematically negative-tested with real `auth.uid()`s. **Never grant `anon` table access** тАФ it would defeat every RLS policy.
- Backend wiring (Supabase) тАФ **in progress.** Design ratified in `reference/backend-schema-design.md`; built in phases (cross-cutting locks тЖТ page-builder design pass тЖТ non-builder migrations тЖТ builder family тЖТ real auth тЖТ surface wiring тЖТ integrations).
- ~~Error-handling pattern тАФ decide on first real use.~~ **Resolved** (Phase 0.5): `Result<T>` + discriminated `AppError` in `src/lib/errors.ts`. See the Code-conventions "Error handling" line + backend-schema-design.md ┬з8.
- ~~**`SettingsPanel` тАФ second-use trigger.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 5 session B): every settings tab page now uses the extracted `components/shared/settings/SettingsPanel`. Don't re-inline the `Card`+`CardContent` pattern in new tab pages тАФ use `SettingsPanel`.
- **`InkHero` тАФ evaluated at six instances (Phase 6 ┬╖ Cluster 6 ┬╖ Session 1a); verdict: styling recipe, not a component.** Six ink-hero-style components exist (`IntegrationProgressHero`, `BillingPlanCard`, `TicketsHero`, `LeadsHero`, `IntegrationMatrixHero`, `FunnelHero`). The structure-vs-styling call: only **3 of 6** share the canonical `[tag][headline][subtitle] | [side]` structure (`TicketsHero` + `LeadsHero` are near-identical twins; `IntegrationMatrixHero` matches if its stat tiles are treated as a generic `right` payload). The other three are genuinely different shapes тАФ a progress-bar row (`IntegrationProgressHero`), a plan-meta line + action (`BillingPlanCard`), a back-link + meta rows + version pill + `FunnelAggCard` + radial flourish (`FunnelHero`). A unified `InkHero` component would need optional slots for all of those тАФ the grab-bag this decision exists to prevent. What IS broadly shared is *styling chrome*: the `bg-ink тАж text-paper` surface and especially the rust mono-pill tag (near-identical in 5 of 6). **So: consolidate as a `cn()` styling recipe (`inkHero*` helpers), NOT a component.** The recipe landed in **Session 1b** as `lib/ink-hero.ts` (`inkHeroSurface()` + `INK_HERO_TAG_CLASS`), first consumed by `ClientHubHero`; existing heroes adopt it opportunistically when next touched тАФ no churn-migration of five shipped surfaces. **Separate still-open item:** `TicketsHero` + `LeadsHero` are true twins тАФ collapsible to one component independently of this verdict; merge whenever one of them is next touched (not urgent, not bundled into Cluster 6).
- ~~**`LeadRailCard` vs `TicketSideCard` vs booking rail тАФ third use of the white-card-rail pattern.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 6 ┬╖ Cluster 6, first commit): `TicketSideCard` тЖТ `shared/RailCard`, `TicketPropertyRow` тЖТ `shared/RailPropertyRow`; `LeadRailCard` / `LeadRailRowItem` merged in (the `rows` shorthand + `tone`/`accent` row vocabulary absorbed). All four old files deleted, no re-export shims; tickets / leads / bookings detail rails migrated. `RailPropertyRow` carries a `labelStyle: 'plain' | 'mono'` knob to cover the divergent label styling (plain for tickets/bookings, mono for leads rows). See the `shared/` rail-primitives inventory entry.
- ~~**`CalendarClientFilterBar` vs `LeadFilterChips` тАФ second use of the rust-active filter-chip recipe.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 5 ┬╖ Cluster 3 ┬╖ Session A): the third use landed (admin `/automations` client filter) and triggered the extraction. `shared/FilterChips.tsx` is the canonical implementation; both `LeadFilterChips` and `CalendarClientFilterBar` were deleted (no re-export shims) and the two callers (`/leads` admin, `/calendar` admin) were migrated to import `FilterChips` directly. The `LeadFilterChip` / `CalendarClientFilter` data types stay in their feature `types.ts` files тАФ they're structurally `FilterChip`-compatible and TypeScript accepts them. Don't reintroduce per-feature wrappers тАФ use `FilterChips` directly.
- ~~**`CalendarClientTone` vs `LeadClientTone` / `AdminTicketClientTone` тАФ three separate client-tone vocabularies.**~~ **Resolved (Session 7).** Two distinct vocabularies, kept separate by design: leads/tickets pills use muted background tints (`bg-rust/[0.12]` etc. тАФ a pill-tint vocabulary); calendar/booking/automations surfaces use solid per-client identity hex (`#4a7ba6` etc. тАФ an identity-colour vocabulary). The solid-identity map was first extracted to `lib/calendar/tones.ts` (at the booking-detail surface), then **promoted to `lib/clients/tones.ts` in Session 7** when `AutomationFlowMini` became the fourth consumer тАФ `lib/calendar/` was the wrong home for a map automations also needs. `CLIENT_TONE_BG` / `CLIENT_TONE_BORDER_L` are keyed on the superset `ClientTone`; feature modules keep their narrower tone unions (`CalendarClientTone`, `AutomationClientTone`) and index the wider record (the shared-types-with-aliases pattern). The muted pill-tint vocabularies (`LeadClientTone` / `AdminTicketClientTone`) were **deliberately NOT folded in** тАФ same family, different vocabulary, build separately (the discipline the `InkHero` and `LeadTimeline` calls applied; this is the third clean application). Don't reopen тАФ the two vocabularies staying separate is the decided outcome.
- **`BuilderFooterActions` + `EditorFooterActions` both exist тАФ revisit for a shared core if a third footer-actions variant appears.** Built as siblings (not a single conditional component) because the interaction models genuinely differ тАФ wizards do Back/Continue + step-count progress, editors do Back/Disable/Save + auto-save indicator. Same discipline that just paid off with `FilterChips`: extract on the third data point, not the second.
- **Three `1fr + fixed-rail` detail layouts now exist (`TicketDetailLayout` 320px, the inline lead-detail shape 320px, `AutomationEditorLayout` 340px) тАФ revisit layout-shell consolidation.** Separate from the already-parked rail-card consolidation. The widths and surface treatments diverge slightly (the editor canvas is a white card; ticket/lead detail wrap the main col in their own surface), so this isn't a drop-in extraction. Don't act now тАФ get it on the list for a future housekeeping pass (the `TicketSideCard` тЖТ `RailCard` rename it was bundled with is now done; this layout-shell item remains open).
- **Numbered-option-row pattern тАФ `ConflictOptionRow` (booking conflict modal) + `NegativeReviewActionRow` (admin Screen 24) are visually adjacent (Phase 5 ┬╖ Cluster 4 ┬╖ Session A).** Both render a numbered ink/rust-light circle + title + sub + a recommended/selected state. The shapes diverge enough to sibling (the conflict row is 2-column with the recommended state colour-only; the negative-review row is 3-column with a visible "Recommended" pill), so they were intentionally not merged. **Third use тЖТ extract** a generic `NumberedOptionRow` in `shared/` with a `pill?: string` slot.
- ~~**`CampaignActivityCard` vs `LeadTimelineEventRow` тАФ second activity-log pattern.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 6 ┬╖ Cluster 6 ┬╖ Session 1a): evaluated at the third-surface trigger (the overview hub's activity feed). The flat-feed shape was extracted to `shared/ActivityFeed` + `shared/ActivityRow`; `CampaignActivityCard` became a thin adapter over it. `LeadTimeline` was **deliberately left a sibling** тАФ a timeline (dot-spine, scheduled-future pending events, tinted snippet quotes, gapped rows) is a genuinely different structural concern from a flat feed, and folding it in would re-create the optional-slot grab-bag. Flat feeds consolidate; the timeline stays. Don't reopen this тАФ `LeadTimeline` staying separate is the decided outcome, not an unfinished one.

- **GBP review-request delay = 2 hours after job-completion.** Hardcoded in migration `0069`'s booking-completion trigger (`run_after = now() + interval '2 hours'`). The brief reasoned: too soon and the SMS arrives while the tradie is walking back to the van (feels presumptuous, lower review-rate); too late and the experience has faded (also lower review-rate). Two hours is the "evening of the day the work happened" sweet spot for typical-hours residential trades. **Trigger to revisit:** if the conversion rate on the manual-send path (which is immediate) significantly beats the 2-hour auto path, the delay may be wrong for some industries; the `gbp_review_requests.sent_at` + `resulted_in_review_id` columns make the comparison queryable once volume warrants. Also revisit per-client: a 24/7 emergency electrician's job-completion at 3am should NOT fire an SMS at 5am; a quiet-hours guard (using the client's `notification_preferences` quiet hours, which doesn't exist as a per-client column today) would replace the flat 2 hours with "first daytime hour тЙе +2h". Out of scope V1; flag if a customer reports late-night SMS complaints.
- **GBP V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** (1) **One GBP location per client** тАФ `client_gbp_locations` is UNIQUE on `client_id`. A multi-location electrician running two suburbs needs the unique loosened + a `primary` flag; defer until a real customer hits the constraint. (2) **No GBP Posts** тАФ `createPost` is a fast-fail stub in `client.ts`. Local posts are a V1.1 add тАФ useful for SEO once basic review automation is proven. (3) **No insights/analytics view** тАФ `getInsights` stubbed too. The views/searches/actions numbers are a dashboard polish pass after V1 proves out. (4) **No auto-generated review replies** тАФ every reply is human. AI-drafted replies could land in V1.1 but only behind explicit "Draft тЖТ operator approves тЖТ publish" UX (auto-publishing AI replies on customer reviews is a credibility footgun). (5) **Review pull is poll-only** тАФ daily `pg_cron` at 06:00 UTC + on-demand "Sync now". GBP push notifications aren't reliable enough to depend on. (6) **Attribution window = 7 days** тАФ review-request `resulted_in_review_id` link is set only when a review arrives within 7 days of a sent request; longer-window reviews are almost always unprompted. (7) **No "did the link get clicked" wiring yet** тАФ `gbp_review_requests.clicked_at` is in the schema but unwritten in V1 (would need link-tracking through a redirect service). UI displays it as a sentinel when a future session wires it.

- **Wizard field enhancement тАФ accept/reject preview, not auto-replace.** `components/shared/EnhanceableTextarea` shows the AI-enhanced version as a preview card with "Use this тЖТ" / "Keep mine" buttons; nothing replaces the user's wording until they explicitly accept. The earlier `CreateClientModal` offer enhance was auto-replace (the polished text overwrote the textarea immediately, with no preview gate); both the offer and the `funnel_customer_pain` fields now flow through the new component. Rationale: AI enhancement on a wizard brief field is **specificity drawing-out**, not blind rewriting тАФ the operator's wording is the ground truth and the enhanced version is a suggestion they should be able to evaluate against the original. Auto-replace loses the operator's input the moment they click; even if they undo via the textarea's history, the recovery is friction-heavy and a hostile-to-trust UX for "I tried it once and the AI ate my words." Accept/reject costs one extra click on the happy path and preserves agency on the unhappy one. **Trigger to revisit:** if telemetry shows operators almost always accept (>90%) the cost of the extra click starts to outweigh the agency benefit тАФ but telemetry like that doesn't exist yet, so the conservative default stands.

- **Two enhance routes (`/api/enhance-offer` + `/api/enhance-field`) тАФ kept as siblings, not merged.** Both Sonnet-backed, same fallback contract. The offer route's system prompt is a direct-response copywriter polishing offer-paragraph copy for a conversion funnel (the Suby/Sultanic framing). The field route's system prompt is a research-grade copywriter interviewing the owner to draw out specificity (generic across freeform brief fields). The framings genuinely differ тАФ the offer route would be too punchy for a thin pain-moment description, and the field route would be too tentative for an offer paragraph. **Trigger to revisit:** if both prompts converge as we tune them and the offer-specific bits collapse into the generic one, merge тАФ but only after at least a third field shows the field-route framing fits universally. Until then, two routes is the honest answer.

- **Automation overlap / anti-spam suppression rules тАФ DEFERRED (Phase 3).** The automation library has six trigger types per client, and multiple flows can target the same recipient тАФ so a suppression layer is needed (don't double-message, don't send contradicting messages, respect quiet hours). The agreed model: (1) **mutual-exclusion / exit conditions** тАФ entering a state cancels conflicting flows (lead тЖТ booked cancels the 24h follow-up; job completed cancels no-show recovery; a new booking cancels win-back); (2) **priority tiers** тАФ transactional (instant confirm, appointment reminder) > nurture (follow-up, win-back) > reputation (review request); (3) a per-recipient **frequency cap** across all automations + per-channel cooldown; (4) **quiet hours**. It is enforced *at send time*, so it belongs with the **automation execution engine тАФ which does not exist yet** (today the cluster is definition + UI only; nothing sends). When built it fits the existing architecture cleanly: the suppression policy belongs in the **agency policy resolver** (`lib/agency/` тАФ `automationDefaults` is already a declared-but-deferred policy key, agency defaults + per-client overrides), and it needs a **`messaging_events`** send-log table тАФ which would *also* close the automation + campaign performance-metrics gap (sent / delivered / replied counts become real). Build it as its own design pass alongside the execution engine; don't bolt inert config on beforehand.

- ~~**Booking creation / reschedule / recurring write flows тАФ DEFERRED (Phase 3).**~~ **Resolved (Phase 3b).** All three booking-write flows are now wired to live writes (the booking *status* mutations were already done in Phase 3):
  - **Reschedule** тАФ `useRescheduleBooking` (`lib/bookings/queries.tsx`) `UPDATE`s `starts_at`/`ends_at`; `RescheduleModal` carries native date/time inputs seeded from the booking, and the `was`/`now` compare cards are computed (was from the booking, now live from the form). The date/timestamp maths lives in `lib/bookings/time.ts` (`composeTimestamp` + siblings тАФ wall-clock-in-UTC, matching the calendar's UTC accessors).
  - **New booking** тАФ `useCreateBooking` resolves the picked customer (inserting a `customers` row for a quick-add) then INSERTs `bookings`. `NewBookingModal` is a controlled form (job title, `CustomerPicker`, native date/time, service, price, notes). `AddBookingButton` resolves the target client тАФ a client books their own, an operator books the active sub-account, and agency mode disables the button until a client is picked.
  - **Recurring** тАФ `useCreateRecurringSchedule` INSERTs one `recurring_booking_schedules` row + a rolling window of ~10 concrete `bookings`. `computeOccurrences` projects the visit window; `checkRecurringConflicts` overlap-checks it against existing bookings. `/recurring/new` is a controlled form with a live preview, and `ConflictModal` is data-driven from the real overlap result (skip the clashing visits, or cancel).
  - **Customer model** тАФ `CustomerPicker` (`shared/bookings/`) + `useCustomerSearch` (`lib/customers/queries.tsx`, RLS- + per-client-scoped `ilike` lookup; filter-syntax chars stripped). The picker hands back a `SelectedCustomer` (existing id, or a new one the write flow inserts). `useClientId` (`lib/clients/queries.tsx`) resolves a client slug тЖТ UUID.
  - Removed in this pass: the `new-booking-modal.tsx` / `RecurringCustomerHeader` stubs; `recurring-setup.tsx` + `conflict-modal.tsx` trimmed to live shapes; `voltlineRecurring`/`voltlineConflict` deleted.
  - **Still a display stub:** the reschedule SMS preview (no messaging backend). **Still deferred:** a top-up job to extend the recurring window past the seeded ~10 bookings.


- **Funnel publish + approval lane тАФ DONE (A3).** The funnel publish lane is wired in parity with the website lane (`lib/funnel/mutations.ts` Lane A `publishFunnelDraft` + Lane B `submitFunnelForApproval` / `approveFunnelSubmission` / `rejectFunnelSubmission` / `recallFunnelSubmission`; `lib/funnel/queries.tsx` publish-state hooks; `lib/funnel/preflight.ts`; the `/funnels/[id]/review` surface; the operator approvals queue on `/tickets`; Realtime via migration 0046). **Three deliberate divergences from the website lane** тАФ each is a structural difference between websites and funnels, not an omission:
  1. **No force-publish.** The website `ForcePublishMenu` is admin break-glass to skip *preflight blockers*. `force_publish_audit_log` is website-keyed (`website_id NOT NULL`, FK to `websites`) тАФ a funnel force-publish row can't be written without a schema change, which is adjacent to the A1-flagged tenant-check gap. And a funnel is operator-managed (the operator IS the content authority), so a funnel preflight blocker is the operator's own to fix. Funnel publish has no break-glass path. **Future session:** if funnels ever need force-publish, extend `force_publish_audit_log` (nullable `website_id` + a `funnel_id`) and generalise `ForcePublishMenu` to a target union.
  2. **The approval queue is one shared "Approvals" tab.** The `/tickets` approvals tab renders website submissions (`WebsiteApprovalRow`) then funnel submissions (`FunnelApprovalRow`); the count is the sum. Not a separate funnel queue page.
  3. **No commit-message / scheduled-publish fields.** The "publish modal" the A3 brief imagined doesn't exist for websites either тАФ the website publish is a *review surface* (`/website/review`), not a modal, and captures no commit message or scheduled-publish time. The funnel review surface mirrors that: a preflight checklist + a Publish / Submit action, no extra fields.
- **Funnel autosave** was already wired in Session 7 (a funnel-keyed `DraftSlot`); A3 did not change it.

- ~~**Wizard preview (`FunnelLandingPreview`) тЙа funnel editor preview.**~~ **Resolved** тАФ Session 7 (the wizard refactor): `FunnelLandingPreview` + `FunnelPreviewState` + the `previewAfter*` snapshots are deleted. The wizard's Step 5 (`/clients/new/draft`) is a wizard-frame `SectionEditor` walk (`WizardSectionEditor`) rendering the section registry's per-section `<Preview>` components тАФ one preview implementation platform-wide. The wizard now produces an editable `Funnel`; steps 1-4 are single-column Q&A forms, the trust step triggers `generateFunnelStub`. See `builder-design.md ┬з5`. **Still deferred:** the wizard does not yet fold its Q&A answers into a real `GenerationContext` (the stub generation ignores them тАФ same as Session 6's specifics/avoid), and funnel publish/preflight is unbuilt (see the funnel-publish parked item above).

- **Agency vs sub-account two-tier model тАФ `/settings/access`, `/website`, `/dashboard` are the references (Phase 6 ┬╖ Cluster 5тАУ6).** GoHighLevel-style. Workspace context driven by `lib/workspace/workspace-stub.tsx` and switched via `AdminClientPicker`. **Agency mode** = cross-client birds-eye for triage. **Sub-account mode** = drill into one client to make changes. `/settings/access` (Cluster 5 ┬╖ Session 1b) and `/website` (Cluster 5 ┬╖ Session 3) are built native against this тАФ agency mode shows a cross-client overview; sub-account mode renders the active client's content. **Cluster 6 ┬╖ Session 1a added the third reference: `/dashboard`** тАФ `app/dashboard/page.tsx` dispatches on `useIsAgencyMode()`, agency mode тЖТ the cross-client roster (`AdminDashboardContent`), sub-account mode тЖТ the single-client overview hub. **The state-driven dispatch pattern (branch on `useIsAgencyMode()` inside the route, no URL change) now has three precedent points тАФ it is the settled platform pattern; a future fourth surface adopts it, it does not get re-decided.** Their agency-level cross-client matrices live at `/settings/access` (agency view) and `/websites` (admin-only). **Surfaces still agency-only that need sub-account variants when next touched:** `/automations` (admin roster тАФ inline groups don't scale past ~5 clients), `/campaigns` (admin roster тАФ same), `/leads` (admin cross-client inbox is correct as triage; but editing/managing a specific lead should land you in sub-account), `/calendar` (cross-client overview correct as triage; booking-edit work should be sub-account), `/reviews` (per-client cards is OK as a hybrid). **Don't refactor the legacy agency-only roster surfaces now** тАФ adopt the pattern surface-by-surface as scope reaches each one. **Cluster 8** formalised the model тАФ see the `## Agency / sub-account model` section near the top: layered resolution, the closed policy-key union, and `/settings/*` joining the mode-dispatch pattern. **Cluster 9** added the plan layer: the `lib/billing/` plan catalog (Layer 2.5 of the resolution stack), the agency `/settings/plans` catalog editor, and `/settings/billing` sub-account mode (plan assignment + resolved bundle).

- **Auth + capability mechanism тАФ real Supabase Auth (DONE).** User resolution, sign-in, and capability grants are all real Supabase: `user-stub.tsx` (misnamed тАФ see its inventory entry) resolves from `supabase.auth` тЖТ `public.users` тЖТ `capability_grants`; `app/(auth)/login` is a real `signInWithPassword` screen; `<UserProvider>` in `app/layout.tsx` is the real provider. **`DevRoleSwitcher` is deleted**; view-as / user-switching / the four stub users are gone. The agency-policy + billing + invite + roster stores (`lib/agency/*`, `lib/billing/*`, `lib/invites/*`, `lib/auth/roster-store.ts`) hydrate from Supabase via `DataHydrationProvider` (`lib/data/DataHydrationProvider.tsx`, mounted in the root layout тАФ `hydrateClients()` first, then the rest in parallel, re-run on every `onAuthStateChange`). `app/dev/` is down to just `/dev/sections`. The capability layer (`capabilities.ts` / `explainers.ts` / `resolver.ts`) is product code, unchanged. **Editor publish/draft/approval family тАФ also Supabase-wired (PR #41).** `publish-stub.ts` + `draft-stub.ts` deleted; `audit-stub.ts` + `website-approval-stub.ts` collapsed to type-only display modules; `content-drafts.ts` + `queries.tsx` + `mutations.ts` + `snapshot.ts` + `builder-events.ts` are the live Supabase layer; `use-autosave.ts` upserts `content_drafts` rows; `use-publish-state.ts` is a re-export shim over `queries.tsx`. **Owed:** a deliberate cross-tenant RLS validation pass тАФ the policies have not been systematically negative-tested with real `auth.uid()`s across tenants.
- **`app/dev/` convention тАФ off-nav developer utilities.** Routes under `src/app/dev/*` are off-nav dev tools. Only **`/dev/sections`** remains (the section-registry ├Ч brand inspector); `/dev/capabilities`, `/dev/generation-preview`, and `/dev/agency-policy` were removed. Don't add user-facing pages here; don't link to `/dev/*` from production nav.

- **Explainer strings assume the Webnua managed-service relationship.** `src/lib/auth/explainers.ts` hardcodes "your operator" / "your account" in every `disable`-mode tooltip and `request`-mode label. Fine for V1 (single-operator platform). If multi-operator deploys land later (white-label, agency reseller, etc.), swap the hardcoded strings for an `{operatorLabel}` token resolved per workspace before the strings get embedded into hundreds of `<CapabilityGate>` calls downstream. Flag the moment a second deploy scenario shows up.

- **Workspace-governance capabilities (billing, team management, client deletion) are not in the 13-cap builder model.** The capability layer covers page-builder access only; org-governance actions live outside it. This is why the team-invite `PermissionPreview` shows owner and operator as identical тАФ in the builder model they genuinely are; they diverge only on governance. Extending the cap model is **deferred**. When next revisited тАФ likely with the backend pass or the first real billing surface тАФ evaluate adding ~4 new caps (e.g. `manageBilling`, `manageTeam`, `deleteClient`, `viewFinancials`) and update `TEAM_ROLE_CAPABILITIES` in `lib/team/roles.ts` so owner/operator reflect their real divergence. The `PermissionPreview` parity note can then be dropped.

- **Per-client seat limit lives on `/settings/access` sub-account mode тАФ provisional home.** The seat limit is a contract/plan axis (how many users a client's plan permits), distinct from the capability axis (`/settings/access`'s main job). It sits on `/settings/access` sub-account mode because that is the operator's only per-client management surface today тАФ there is no standalone client-record edit surface, and inventing one was rejected as scope creep. It's rendered as a visually-distinct `SettingsSection`, separate from the capability grid, to keep the two axes from blurring. The data layer is home-agnostic: as of Cluster 8 ┬╖ Session 4b the seat limit resolves through the `defaultSeatLimit` policy key (agency default + per-account override) тАФ `lib/clients/seat-limit-stub.ts` is a thin facade over the resolver, and `AdminClient.seatLimit` has been retired. **Cluster 9 landed `/settings/billing` sub-account mode** тАФ the seat-limit *editing control* (`ClientSeatLimitCard`) deliberately stayed on `/settings/access` (it's a per-account override, an Access concern); `/settings/billing` shows the seat limit *resolved, read-only* as part of the assigned plan's bundle. If a future revisit wants the per-account override editable from Billing too, that's a placement call to make then тАФ not a forced move.

- **Client-internal hierarchy is flat for V1 тАФ deferred.** Every client-invited user gets the `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` baseline; the client teammate-invite flow has no in-flow role pick (no co-owner vs member tier). The capability model doesn't currently distinguish a client-internal admin from a regular client user, and inventing a tier to match a UI shape would be the drift the operator-side Step-2 call correctly avoided. When workspace-governance caps land (see the item above), `inviteClientTeammate` becomes a real capability and the client-invite flow can gate it тАФ at which point a client-internal role tier can be designed against a real cap, not a guessed one.

- **`funnel_testimonials` renders placeholders, never AI-generated testimonials.** The wizard captures 0тАУ3 real customer testimonials per funnel; the AI funnel generator (wired in a later session) reads them straight onto the social-proof section. **When the list is empty, the funnel renders an explicit "Your customer reviews will appear here" placeholder** rather than asking Claude to invent quotes тАФ fabricated testimonials are a credibility / consumer-protection foot-gun nothing else in the platform recovers from, and the placeholder is honest about what's missing. The deterministic funnel generator preserves the same behaviour. **Trigger to revisit:** when the GBP integration ships and the platform can auto-pull real Google reviews тАФ empty `funnel_testimonials` can then resolve to real GBP entries at render time instead of a placeholder. Until then: empty = placeholder, full stop.

- **Phase 6 generation fallback policy.** On `/api/generate-site` `503` (key not configured), `site-generation-stub.ts` falls back to the deterministic stub silently тАФ intentional for dev so the create flow works without an `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. On `500` (real generation failure), the error is now thrown and surfaced in `CreateClientModal`'s error pane via the server's `{ name, status, detail }` body тАФ no more invisible stub-degradation when Claude actually fails. Network throws still fall back (with a `console.warn`) so a transient connectivity blip doesn't hard-fail the flow. **Trigger to revisit:** if operators report seeing stub-quality copy in production, check `generation_log` for matching field-level fallback entries тАФ every real generation writes one row per fallback field (see commit `feat(phase-6): write generation_log entries from generate-live.ts`).

- **Phase 6 generation TypeError тАФ RESOLVED (three commits).** Server-side `/api/generate-site` was crashing with `TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'includes')` on `def.allowedContainers` inside the registry filter. Root cause was structural: every section file under `sections/*.tsx` is `'use client'` (because it ships React Fields/Preview components), and Next's RSC bundler replaces all 'use client' exports with `registerClientReference` stubs in the server bundle тАФ so the `SECTION_REGISTRY` array the server route imported was an array of stub functions, not real section definitions. PR #58 surfaced the masked 500 from the modal; the structural fix introduced `sections/registry-meta.ts` (no 'use client', SSOT for metadata) and switched `generation-prompt.ts` + `generation-stub.ts` to read `SECTION_REGISTRY_META`. The editor continues to read `SECTION_REGISTRY` (the full definition with Fields/Preview) тАФ only the server consumers moved. **Round two (this commit)** caught the latent risk the first fix flagged: `fillHeaderSection` / `fillFooterSection` (the only other server-reachable functions in `generation-stub.ts`, called from the route handler to produce site chrome) were still calling `headerSection.defaultData()` / `footerSection.defaultData()` directly тАФ same stub problem, different call site. The fix added an optional `defaultDataValues: Readonly<Record<string, unknown>>` field to `SectionMeta` (a static snapshot of the section's `defaultData()` output, populated only for `headerMeta` + `footerMeta` since they're the only server-reachable consumers today), and switched the two fill helpers to read from `getSectionMeta('header'/'footer')?.defaultDataValues`. The unused `headerSection` / `footerSection` imports in `generation-stub.ts` were removed. Three commits in total: `433d850` (introduce `SECTION_REGISTRY_META`), `c6ffaf0` (switch server consumers + section files re-import metadata), and this one (eliminate `defaultData()` call sites on the server path).

- **Section metadata server/client boundary.** Section files are `'use client'` because they ship React components. Server-side generation consumers MUST import from `sections/registry-meta.ts`, never from `sections/*.tsx` directly (or from `sections/index.ts`'s `SECTION_REGISTRY`, which transitively imports the `'use client'` modules). The `SECTION_REGISTRY_META` array is the source of truth for metadata; the full section definitions in `sections/index.ts` (`SECTION_REGISTRY` + `getSectionDefinition`) exist for the editor and other client-only consumers. **This applies to default DATA as well as metadata** тАФ server code must never call `xxxSection.defaultData()` on a section import (those exports are client-reference stubs on the server). When a server-reachable path needs a section's defaults, populate `defaultDataValues` on that section's `*Meta` entry in `registry-meta.ts` and read from there (`getSectionMeta(type)?.defaultDataValues`). Today only `headerMeta` and `footerMeta` carry `defaultDataValues` because `fillHeaderSection` / `fillFooterSection` are the only server-reachable consumers; the other fillers (`fillHero`, `fillOffer`, etc.) live in `generation-stub.ts` but are only invoked from client-side fallback paths (`generateSync` reached from `/website/new` and the create-client modal). **Trigger to revisit:** (1) if section schemas grow large enough that the duplication-via-spread pattern (metadata in `registry-meta.ts`, `defaultData` function in the section module) becomes lossy тАФ e.g. if the field-key list per section grows enough that drift between `defaultDataKeys` and a section's actual `DEFAULTS` becomes a maintenance problem, move the `DEFAULTS` data into `registry-meta.ts` too and have the section files import them; (2) if a new server-reachable code path needs another section's defaults, add `defaultDataValues` to that section's `*Meta` first тАФ do NOT add `defaultData()` calls to server code.

- **Funnel-offer generator тАФ Sonnet 4.6 (not Opus), editable after generation.** The four-field funnel offer (`/api/generate-offer`) uses Sonnet rather than Opus: the task is short, structured, well-prompt-able copy тАФ `headline тЙд12 words`, `promise тЙд25`, `risk-reversal тЙд15`, `cta тЙд6` тАФ Sonnet handles this fluently and Opus pricing is not justified for ~150 output tokens. **Trigger to revisit:** if operators report Sonnet drafts losing the brief's specifics (treating "burst pipe at 9pm" as generic), or repeatedly using banned filler ("comprehensive", "leverage", etc.) the prompt explicitly forbids, escalate to Opus and keep the same prompt. The 13-rule prompt + the explicit ban list should make Sonnet competent here; Opus is a fallback, not a default. **Editable-after-generation UX:** the wizard renders the four fields as editable inputs the moment the call returns тАФ user can accept, edit any field, or regenerate. The justification is recovery: if Sonnet drifts on any single field, edit takes seconds; if we made the offer non-editable, the only recovery would be regenerating the entire thing or fixing it later in the editor. **Trigger to revisit:** if telemetry shows operators rarely edit (тЙд10% touch any field), reconsider making it non-editable to reduce decision fatigue тАФ but that requires telemetry we do not yet collect. Until then, editable is the safe default.

- **Funnel vs offer generator model choice тАФ Opus on funnel, Sonnet on offer.** The two AI-generation entry points the wizard runs split deliberately on model. **Offer** (`/api/generate-offer`) uses **Sonnet 4.6**: four short structured strings (~150 output tokens total) тАФ Opus is overkill, and the field-level editable-after-generation UX means a drift is recoverable in-flow. **Funnel** (`/api/generate-funnel`) uses **Opus 4.7**: seven full sections of conversion copy in one structured response, the section copy lands directly into the published draft (no field-by-field accept gate), and the funnel is the actual money-conversion surface тАФ quality matters more than per-call cost. Same `503` тЖТ deterministic-fallback shape; same `500` тЖТ `AppError` unmasking; same `generation_log` observability. **Trigger to revisit:** if Opus latency on the funnel call exceeds operator tolerance during the in-modal generation phase (sustained > 60s P95), or if Sonnet starts handling extended-thinking conversion copy at the same quality bar Opus does today, evaluate dropping the funnel to Sonnet тАФ but keep the model id behind a single `MODEL` const in `generate-funnel-live.ts`, not behind a feature flag. **Anthropic constraints тАФ two different thinking shapes:** Opus 4.7 only accepts `thinking: { type: 'adaptive' }` (no `budget_tokens`); passing `{ type: 'enabled', budget_tokens: N }` returns a 400 `"thinking.type.enabled" is not supported for this model. Use \"thinking.type.adaptive\"тАж`. Sonnet 4.6 still supports `{ type: 'enabled', budget_tokens }` тАФ and when used, requires `max_tokens > budget_tokens` or returns a 400 `invalid_request_error` (the offer route's original `max_tokens: 2000 / budget: 2000` hit this; fix was `max_tokens: 4000`). New routes must match the constraint to the model: adaptive on Opus, enabled+budget (with `max_tokens > budget`) on Sonnet.

- **Prompt-content fixes for reported symptoms тАФ applied directly to website + funnel prompts.** Three reported generation-quality symptoms тАФ (1) funnel copy mostly blank except headlines, (2) `headlineAccent` / `titleAccent` duplicated with the headline rather than treated as a second-line accent, (3) layout drift (left-align when center expected; missing icons) тАФ were addressed in `src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts` + `src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts` by adding three pieces of content: a per-section `SECTION_SHAPE_CATALOG` that documents variant-key enum values + item-array element object shapes; a `SHARED_FIELD_NOTES` block emitted in both prompts that explains the heading-accent semantic, lists the 74 curated icon ids, declares the item-id rule, and explains the `theme` object shape; and reinforcing bullets in each prompt's "Rules:" list. The semantic for `headlineAccent` is **an optional SECOND LINE in the accent colour beneath the headline**, NOT a substring of the headline (the section modules' in-editor helper "Optional second line тАФ rendered in the brand accent colour." is the source of truth; the original task brief had this wrong). The offer (`/api/generate-offer`) and enhance (`/api/enhance-field` + `/api/enhance-offer`) prompts were NOT touched тАФ none of the three symptoms implicated them. **Trigger to revisit:** if the same three symptoms recur after this fix, the next step is worked-example shots (a fully-populated section JSON inline in the system prompt) тАФ the catalog approach taken here is the lighter-weight option. Subsequent prompt-quality sessions should address the other audit findings (banned-word consolidation, copy-vs-layout via `capabilityHints`, voice on offer/enhance, shared base persona).

- **Offer pricing тАФ model cannot invent prices; runtime safeguard retries once on detection.** Two layers in `src/app/api/generate-offer/route.ts`: (1) the system prompt carries explicit guidance тАФ when the brief carries no price, use qualitative language ("honest upfront pricing", "free quote, no obligation", "fixed-price quote on the spot") instead of inventing a number; a specific dollar / euro / pound figure may appear ONLY if the operator's brief contains that exact figure; (2) after the first Claude call returns, a `PRICE_PATTERN` regex (currency symbols next to a digit, or a number followed by a currency word тАФ "dollars", "euros", "GBP", etc.) scans all four returned fields. If a price appears in the output AND no price was in the brief, the route retries ONCE with a stronger no-pricing instruction prepended to the user message. Cap is one retry per call тАФ no retry storms. If the retry also invents a price, the retry result is shipped with a `console.warn` (no better option; the user can edit any field in the wizard). **Observability is console-only** тАФ the `generation_log` table requires `client_id` (NOT NULL), but offer generation runs BEFORE the client row exists, so the route can't write there (matches the existing `generate-seo` / `enhance-offer` / `enhance-field` precedent). **Trigger to revisit:** if retries fail repeatedly across operators (visible only via the second `console.warn` in production logs), escalate to surfacing `AppError` in the wizard so the operator sees what happened, or wire a separate observability sink (e.g. a `generation_diagnostics` table without the `client_id` constraint).

- **Section themes тАФ brand defaults apply via renderer; model does not output theme.** Sections occasionally rendered with text colour matching the background, making content invisible. Root cause: the model picked `theme` values per section that didn't have guaranteed contrast against the section's text colour. Three layers of fix: (1) the model is explicitly told NOT to emit a `theme` field тАФ `SHARED_FIELD_NOTES` (`src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`) opens with a "Section themes" appendix explaining themes are applied automatically by the renderer from the brand palette; the website + funnel system prompts each carry an explicit "Do NOT output a `theme` field" rule in their "Rules:" lists; the previous "Theme objects" appendix is removed and `theme` no longer appears in the variant-keys hint list; (2) the funnel system prompts' "Populate only `theme`, `eyebrow`, `heading`" form-section rule is now "Populate only `eyebrow`, `heading`" (the renderer themes the form section too); (3) defence in depth тАФ the validation pipeline (`runValidationPipeline` in `generation-stub.ts` and `validateAndAssemble` in `generate-funnel-live.ts`) discards any model-emitted `theme` value before the section lands in the editor. The discard is logged as a `FallbackLogEntry` with `reason: 'invalid'` and `fieldName: 'theme'` so the website route's `generation_log` writer can track whether the model is still emitting theme after the prompt change. **Trigger to revisit:** if `generation_log` entries with `field_name='theme'` and `reason='invalid'` show the model still emitting theme at meaningful rates, harden the prompt further (worked-example shots showing a section JSON without a `theme` key). If branded sections feel visually monotonous because every section uses the same brand-default colours, introduce a small per-section variant enum (e.g. `surface: 'primary' | 'secondary' | 'neutral' | 'dark'`) the model can choose from instead of restoring full theme freedom тАФ the renderer would still map each enum value to a known-contrast pair from the brand palette.

- **Worked examples тАФ all four AI generation prompts use the same fictional anchor business (Voltline Electrical, residential electrical contractor in Perth coastal suburbs тАФ Cottesloe, Mosman Park, Claremont; owner Mark, 15 years on the tools; differentiators are fixed-quote pricing and same-day emergency response).** The website prompt (`src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`) carries a six-section home page; the funnel step-1 system prompt (`src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts`) carries a seven-section lead-capture page in the Suby/Sultanic order; the funnel step-2 system prompt carries a four-section qualification page; the offer prompt (`src/app/api/generate-offer/route.ts`) carries a complete four-field offer; the enhance-field prompt (`src/app/api/enhance-field/route.ts`) carries a before/after pair for the `funnel_customer_pain` field. The example is shared deliberately so the model sees a consistent standard across the whole generation pipeline, and each example carries an explicit "do NOT copy these specifics" guard at the end. Every JSON example was validated against the section-type registry (`SECTION_REGISTRY_META`) + the curated 74-icon vocabulary (`section-icons.ts`) before commit тАФ section types, icon ids, and variant enum values all resolve cleanly. **Trigger to revisit:** if generated output starts to resemble Voltline's specifics (Perth coastal suburbs, electrician, 2-hour response, "Mark", EC10437, named suburbs) for non-electrician briefs, the model is over-indexing on the example and the examples should be diversified across multiple trades (e.g. a plumber example for the funnel step-2 prompt, a cleaner example for the website prompt). Until that telemetry appears, a single shared anchor is the higher-leverage choice тАФ it teaches the quality bar once rather than diluting it across five mediocre examples.

- **Copy vs layout field separation in generation prompts.** The website + funnel prompts split each section's `defaultDataKeys` into a COPY bucket and a LAYOUT bucket using `SectionMeta.capabilityHints.copyFields` as the authoritative source (with a name-based heuristic fallback for any future section type that ships without hints тАФ see `partitionFields` in `src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`). The per-section catalog entry lists copy fields first under "Copy fields (populate with specific, on-brand content):" and layout fields second under "Layout fields (omit unless the brief specifically requires a variation тАФ defaults apply):". The main rules in both the cached website system prompt (`src/lib/website/generate-live.ts`) and both funnel system prompts (`src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts`) were reworded to match: populate every COPY field; do NOT specify a LAYOUT field unless the brief justifies a variation. Also: both funnel system prompts now carry an explicit "do NOT output a `fields` array on the form section" instruction in the form section's section-plan brief (the form's `fields[]` is built deterministically in code and was already discarded by `validateAndAssemble`, but the prompt now says so up front so the model doesn't waste tokens drafting an array that will be thrown away). **Trigger to revisit:** if the model consistently fails to specify a layout variation that would improve a page (operators reporting consistently centred or consistently left-aligned output when the page wanted the other), soften the omit-unless-required language or let the model choose for specific sections тАФ but only after telemetry, not by guess. The opposite failure (model invents layout variations the brief doesn't justify) was the symptom this change targets; the change should make that strictly less likely. Cross-check with `generation_log` "missing" entries on layout keys тАФ a sharp rise after this change is the expected signature; a sharp rise on copy keys would mean the partition is mis-classifying and would justify reopening.

- **Funnel lead threading uses ?lead=<id> URL parameter from step 1 to step 2.** `/api/forms/submit` returns `{ ok: true, leadId }` on a new-lead insert. `FormBlock`'s `handlePublicSubmit` reads `leadId` off the response and тАФ when `form.afterSubmit.kind === 'nextStep'` тАФ appends `?lead=<leadId>` to `publicSubmit.nextStepHref` before redirecting. On step 2's mount the same `FormBlock` reads `?lead=` from `window.location.search` (UUID-validated against `UUID_RE`) and posts it as `existingLeadId` on the next submit. The route validates: must be a syntactic UUID (malformed тЖТ 400); must resolve to a lead with the same `clientId` posted in the body (cross-tenant guard тАФ wrong-client and not-found collapse to one 400 message so neither leaks lead existence). Per-funnel scoping is the *strongest* check the current schema permits тАФ `leads` carries no `funnel_id` column today; when it does, tighten the guard. **Trigger to revisit:** if users complain about lost step-2 data, check whether the URL parameter is being stripped тАФ likely culprits are an aggressive referrer policy on the funnel domain, a browser extension stripping query params, or a custom step-2 redirect rule between step 1's submit and step 2's render. The parameter is **the only** mechanism stitching the two submissions; nothing else (cookie / localStorage / server session) carries the link today. A more robust alternative тАФ a short-lived signed cookie set at the submit endpoint тАФ is the next step if the URL approach breaks in practice. The `?lead=` value is a server-generated UUID and is rate-limited at 8 submits/IP/min, but it does ride the URL bar; treat it as a low-secrecy session token, not a stable identifier.
- **Funnel analytics gaps that remain after lead threading тАФ RESOLVED for the rollup + filter shape, partly deferred for attribution and reconciliation.** This was the original audit punchlist; the resolved-vs-deferred split is:
  - **Rollup step-granularity тАФ RESOLVED (migration 0042).** `analytics_funnel_daily` now keys on `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label, page_ref)`; step-1 and step-2 `page_view` / `form_start` / `form_submit` rows are distinct. `fetchFunnelStepBreakdown(surfaceId, pageRefs)` reads the per-step axis; surfaced on `/funnels/[id]` per prototype Screen 23.
  - **`lead_status` enum stays as it is тАФ deliberately.** Adding a `partial` / `qualified` value was the original proposed close; it was rejected once the operator-facing framing landed ("every lead is a lead тАФ completion is a filter axis, not a quality grade"). Completion is derived at read time from `lead_events` (`deriveCompletion` in `lib/leads/queries.tsx`); the `LeadCompletion` field is surfaced on the row records for the future automation engine's read but is not exposed as a user-facing inbox filter (the user-facing axis is `source_kind` instead тАФ see below). Persisting completion as a column was considered and rejected тАФ the derivation is cheap, lead_events is already in the inbox select, and the column would need a refresh path on every `form_submitted` insert. Revisit only if query cost becomes a problem (e.g. operator dashboards filter on completion at scale).
  - **Inbox source column тАФ RESOLVED (different axis than originally planned).** The original Session B plan added a `LeadCompletionFilter` (in-progress vs completed) to the inbox; that filter was sunset on operator feedback ("Google Analytics isn't the framing тАФ we track in-app тАФ and the operator cares about *where the lead came from*, not how far through the funnel they got"). The replacement is a categorical Source column on every inbox row (website / funnel / meta) backed by the new `leads.source_kind` column (migration 0043) тАФ surfaced via `LeadSourcePill`. `meta` is reserved for the Meta lead-ads integration. The `LeadCompletion` derivation stays in code for the automation engine; the inbox just doesn't filter on it. `LeadCompletionFilter.tsx` was deleted.
  - **Drop-off detection тАФ partly resolved (the read-time signal), execution worker still deferred.** `isLeadDroppedOff(events)` returns true for a lead with only one `form_submitted` older than `LEAD_DROP_OFF_HOURS` (24h V1). This is what the future automation engine reads to decide whether to fire a follow-up nudge тАФ but no scheduled worker currently calls it. The hook is here; the cron is Phase 8 work (automation execution engine тАФ see the "Automation overlap / anti-spam suppression rules" parked decision).
  - **Funnel-to-lead attribution тАФ RESOLVED (migration 0044).** `leads.source_funnel_id` (nullable FK to `funnels`, set-null on delete) is now written by `/api/forms/submit` for every funnel submission тАФ the public renderer threads the funnel UUID through `PublicFormSubmit.funnelId` тЖТ POST body тЖТ cross-tenant-guarded insert. `getBookedFromFunnelCount` runs a real count (`source_funnel_id = funnelId` + `status in ('booked', 'completed')` + capture window) and the funnel-detail hero "booked from this funnel" tile renders live numbers instead of `тАФ`. See "Funnel-to-lead attribution" below for the resolved entry.
  - **`leads.submission_id`** is written but never read тАФ same as before; reconciliation job is still deferred. Not blocking anything visible today.
- **Website-side analytics aggregation closed (migrations 0040 + 0041); funnel rollup step-granularity closed by migration 0042.** Migrations 0040 + 0041 close the analytics-audit ┬з3 / ┬з4 website-side gaps: `form_abandon` rolls into `form_abandoned`, scroll thresholds at 25 / 50 / 75 / 90 each roll into a distinct stage (50% kept as the canonical `engaged` label so existing read-layer + dashboard surfaces stay wired with zero migration on the consumer side), and per-CTA click distinction is preserved via an `element_label` column on `analytics_funnel_daily` extending the PK to `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label)`. Two implementation-shape decisions: **(1) scroll-stage naming** тАФ `engaged` (50%) deliberately keeps its existing name rather than being renamed to `scrolled_50`, because every existing consumer of `SurfaceFunnelTotals.engaged` (dashboard conversion funnel, hub funnel bars) already trusts that stage; the new thresholds are `scrolled_25 / scrolled_75 / scrolled_90` and pair cleanly. Re-evaluate the naming inconsistency only if a third surface needs to iterate every threshold from a single key list. **(2) per-element click rollup approach** тАФ Option A (extend the rollup PK with `element_label`; non-click stages write `''`) over Option B (separate per-element rollup table). One table, one read path; `fetchSurfaceFunnelTotals` keeps working because summing across element_label rows produces the same per-stage count when consumers don't care about the label, and the new `fetchSurfaceClickBreakdown` reads the same table filtered to `stage = 'cta_click'` for the top-N. **┬з2.2 funnel rollup step-granularity тАФ RESOLVED (migration 0042).** Same chosen shape as the element_label approach: extend the existing rollup PK with `page_ref` (empty-string sentinel matches the element_label convention), rather than introduce a separate per-step rollup table. The pre-aggregation read paths (`fetchSurfaceFunnelTotals`) continue to work тАФ summing across `page_ref` rows reproduces the pre-migration per-stage totals, so "total form submits across the funnel" surfaces don't break; the new per-step read uses `fetchFunnelStepBreakdown(surfaceId, pageRefs)`. The dashboard's conversion-funnel and hub bars stay as-is (per-client aggregate, not per-step); per-step rendering lives on `/funnels/[id]` per prototype Screen 23. **Trigger to revisit:** the prototype's step-3 footer rows (SMS SENT / SHOWED UP / NO-SHOW) are not funnel-tracker data тАФ they need a bookings-side read keyed to a thanks-step `page_ref` lookup that doesn't exist yet. Adding them is its own follow-up, not blocked on schema.

- **Funnel-to-lead attribution тАФ RESOLVED (migration 0044).** `leads.source_funnel_id uuid` (nullable, FK to `public.funnels`, `on delete set null`) is now the attribution column. Written at lead creation in `/api/forms/submit` when `surfaceKind === 'funnel'` and a `funnelId` body field is present (cross-tenant guard: the funnel must belong to the posted `clientId`); website submissions leave it NULL. The public renderer threads it through cleanly тАФ `PublicSiteRenderer` takes a `funnelId` prop on the `funnel` case (sourced from `resolveSite`'s `tracking.surfaceId`), which lands on the `publicSubmit` context's `funnelId` field; `FormBlock` includes it in the POST body. `getBookedFromFunnelCount` (`lib/analytics/queries.tsx`) runs the real query: one count over `leads` filtered by `source_funnel_id = funnelId` + `status in ('booked', 'completed')` + `created_at` within the window (default 7-day matching the funnel hero's "Funnel performance ┬╖ 7 days"; the optional `dateRange` parameter overrides). The funnel-detail hero "booked from this funnel" tile renders live numbers. Leads created before this migration carry NULL and are correctly excluded. **Editor test-submit attribution is intentionally NOT wired** тАФ `submitLead` and `FormTestSubmitContext` don't carry a `funnelId`; test leads from a funnel preview record `source_kind = 'funnel'` but `source_funnel_id = NULL`. Test traffic is rare enough in production analytics that the additional plumbing wasn't worth this session; thread `funnelId` through `FormTestSubmitContext` + `submitLead` later if test traffic starts polluting the count.

- **Funnel lead completion state тАФ derived at read time, not persisted.** `LeadCompletion` (`'in_progress' | 'completed'`) is derived in `lib/leads/queries.tsx#deriveCompletion` by counting `form_submitted` events on a lead's `lead_events` timeline (тЙе2 тЖТ completed, else in-progress). NOT a persisted column on `leads` тАФ the derivation is cheap, `lead_events` is already in the inbox select, and a persisted column would need a refresh path on every `form_submitted` insert. NOT a user-facing lead label / quality grade either тАФ operators see "Leads captured: N" as the headline metric (analytics-audit ┬з5.1); the completion field is for the inbox filter ("Show only leads still in progress" тЖТ still actionable for a follow-up nudge) and for the future automation engine's read. **Trigger to revisit:** if a dashboard surface needs to filter by completion at high cardinality (тЙе10k leads) and the per-row derivation becomes a query-cost concern, persist it as a column and refresh from a `lead_events` `AFTER INSERT` trigger. Not warranted today.

- **24-hour drop-off threshold for funnel runs is a V1 choice.** `LEAD_DROP_OFF_HOURS = 24` in `lib/leads/queries.tsx` is the threshold `isLeadDroppedOff(events)` uses to classify a single-`form_submitted` lead as "dropped" rather than "still in progress" тАФ read by future automation logic (the "send a follow-up nudge" decision; Phase 8). The inbox filter does NOT use this threshold (a step-1-only lead is "in progress" regardless of age тАФ the filter is about operator action, not lead quality, so age doesn't change the framing). **Trigger to revisit:** raise if operators report leads being marked dropped when they're actually still in-progress; lower or remove if leads sit in-progress indefinitely. The 24-hour pick is an even split between "give the visitor time to come back later that day" and "don't wait so long the nudge is creepy" тАФ re-evaluate once Phase 8's automation execution engine lands and the actual nudge cadence is calibrated.

- **Branch-name vs scope drift тАФ discipline-restoration rule.** During the Phase 4тАУ6 build window (PRs #41тАУ#55, audited in `reference/drift-recovery/pr-deep-audit.md`), branch names frequently failed to describe the shipped work тАФ most notably `debug-admin-access` shipping the entire form-builder feature (PR #46) and `review-dev-plan` shipping the Phase 6 Claude wiring (PR #47). Going forward: if work scope changes meaningfully during a session, **rename the branch** or **state the actual shipped scope in the first line of the PR description**. Merge commit titles are the authoritative record; branch names are advisory only. **Trigger to revisit:** if a future audit shows the pattern recurring, escalate to mandatory PR-description-first-line scope statements.

- **RLS test coverage is mandatory for new RLS policies.** Section A's cross-tenant validation pass built a permanent negative-test harness (`tests/rls/`, `pnpm test:rls`, doc: `reference/rls-test-suite.md`) and closed three holes (migration `0045`). Going forward: **any PR that adds or changes an RLS-protected resource MUST add or update the corresponding tests in `tests/rls/` in the same PR.** A new tenant-scoped table тЖТ seed a disposable row in `context.mjs` + a `clientScoped`/`childCrossTenant` call; a new operator-only / per-viewer / capability-gated policy тЖТ explicit suite tests. The harness is a negative-test harness тАФ verify persisted state through a verifier client, never trust the attacker's error code (an `INSERT...RETURNING` can raise `42501` while the row was written; see migration `0028`). **Two structural items deferred to a future session** (see `reference/rls-test-suite.md` ┬з4): `force_publish_audit_log_insert` has no website/tenant check (operator-internal, low severity тАФ a junior operator could write an audit row for an out-of-scope website); and `signup_submissions` exists in the DB with RLS policies but has **no migration in `supabase/migrations/`** (migration drift тАФ its policies are safe, but the table should be captured in a migration). **Cross-agency isolation** is not testable on the current single-agency deployment тАФ the operative boundaries are client tenant isolation and junior-operator workspace scoping, both covered.

- **Twilio SMS тАФ V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** The Twilio SMS session shipped one-way alphanumeric SMS sending; each stop-short below is a conscious V1 call. (1) **Per-segment cost is a single flat constant** тАФ `SMS_SEGMENT_COST_EUR = 0.05` (`lib/sms/pricing.ts`), a representative IE/UK transactional rate, NOT a real per-country rate table. The estimate ("~тВм0.05/send") and the `sms_messages.cost_eur` column are good-enough operator-facing approximations. **Trigger to revisit:** when volume or multi-country destinations matter, replace the constant with a per-country rate lookup. (2) **No two-way SMS** тАФ alphanumeric senders are one-way by nature; there is no inbound webhook, no SMS inbox. Two-way is WhatsApp / a direct call, deferred. (3) **No per-customer phone numbers** тАФ one alphanumeric sender per client; long-code/short-code numbers are not modelled. (4) **Sender registration** тАФ `registerSenderID()` adds the alphanumeric string to the Messaging Service AlphaSender pool (instant, usable in non-regulated countries). The regulated-country Sender ID *registration* (the genuine "1тАУ3 business days" carrier process) is completed by the operator in the Twilio Console тАФ the app does not drive it; "Refresh status" polls Twilio and flips the row to `approved` once the AlphaSender resolves. (5) **Webhook status updates are last-write-wins** тАФ not ordering-aware; an out-of-order older callback could in theory overwrite a newer status. Transactional SMS statuses arrive in order in practice; revisit with a status-rank guard only if operators report a row reverting. (6) **The lead-acknowledgment SMS fires only from the public `/api/forms/submit` flow**, not from the editor test-submit (`submitLead`) тАФ a test submission must not fire a real customer SMS. (7) **`{{client.responseTime}}`** has no schema column тАФ the `send_sms` handler defaults it to `'1 hour'`; override per-send via the job payload's `contextOverrides`. (8) **`sms_messages` / `sms_templates` / `client_sms_senders` have no `tests/rls/` coverage** тАФ the "new RLS resource тЖТ new RLS test" rule (above) is triggered by `0059`/`0060`'s new tables; a follow-up RLS-harness pass should add `clientScoped` probes for all three (all are operator-SELECT-or-own-client + service-role-write, low risk, but the rule stands). (9) **Verification gap:** this session could not run the live test SMS / webhook round-trip the brief asks for тАФ no Twilio credentials, no deployed app in the build environment. The pure modules (validator / renderer / estimator) are fully exercisable offline; the Twilio-dependent paths need a deployment with credentials.

- **Meta Ads тАФ V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** V1 shipped the per-tenant Meta Ads integration with a deliberate division of labour: **Webnua handles connection + ingest + observability**; **the operator builds campaigns directly in Meta Ads Manager** (the customer's OAuth grant gives Webnua business-manager access). (1) **No in-app campaign builder** тАФ `LaunchMetaCampaignButton` deep-links to `business.facebook.com/adsmanager/manage/campaigns?act={id}` for the connected ad account. The previous in-app wizard (template picker + Page picker + budget + privacy + landing URL) + the 5-step orchestrator + the 9 trade templates + the `launch` route action were removed once this V1 model settled. The `create*` API functions in `client.ts` are kept exported (un-called) for a future in-app launch path if one ever ships. (2) **Campaign ingest is wired; lead-form ingest is not.** `meta_sync_campaigns` (server: `meta-ads/job-handlers.ts`; cron: migration `0075`, hourly at minute 7; immediate trigger after ad-account pick + the "тЖ╗ Sync campaigns" button) discovers campaigns built in Ads Manager and upserts both `public.campaigns` + `meta_campaigns`. **`meta_lead_form_id` is null on ingest** тАФ discovering lead forms means walking the campaign тЖТ ad-set тЖТ ad тЖТ creative chain (or pulling per-Page), which is a separate follow-up. Without it, `meta_sync_leads` does not pull leads for Ads-Manager-launched campaigns; the campaigns themselves + their insights + their on-Meta posture appear correctly. (3) **One ad account per client** тАФ `client_meta_ad_accounts` is UNIQUE on `client_id`. An agency client managing multiple ad accounts needs the unique loosened + a `primary` flag (same forcing function as GBP); defer until the first real customer hits the constraint. (4) **тВм200 month-1 ad-credit funding is manual** тАФ the `meta_campaigns.created_via` tagging (`webnua_month_1` / `webnua_ongoing` / `external`) is set to `external` on every ingest (Webnua didn't launch them); manual operator accounting drives the тВм200 transfer from Webnua to the customer's ad account out-of-band (Stripe Transfer / SEPA + the customer manually tops up their Meta funding source). V2 will automate via Meta's funding APIs (which themselves require additional App Review). (5) **Per-row sparkline = lead counts, not spend** тАФ the admin `/campaigns` row sparkline shows the last 14 days of daily lead counts. Spend trends live on the client deep-dive's 4-week chart only. (6) **`client_meta_ad_accounts` / `meta_campaigns` / `meta_ads_insights` / `meta_lead_forms` have no `tests/rls/` coverage** тАФ the "new RLS resource тЖТ new RLS test" rule (above) is triggered by migrations `0070`тАУ`0073`; a follow-up RLS-harness pass should add `clientScoped` probes for all four. (7) **Verification gap:** this session could not run the live test (connect a real customer's Meta ad account, verify insights + leads syncing) тАФ Meta business verification + App Review for the sensitive scopes (`ads_management`, `business_management`, `pages_manage_ads`, `leads_retrieval`) is the operator's responsibility and takes weeks. Until App Review approves Webnua for Advanced Access on each scope, only test users added on the Developer dashboard can connect. The pure modules (status mapping, lead-data extraction) work offline; every Meta-dependent path needs the App approved + a customer's real ad account.
- **Stripe billing тАФ V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** The Stripe billing session shipped subscription billing (тВм299/month) and deliberately stopped short in several places; each is a conscious V1 call, not an omission. (1) **The тВм99 + тВм200 month-1 split is UI copy, not Stripe.** Stripe charges a flat тВм299 every month; the "тВм99 platform fee + тВм200 Meta ad credit" framing lives only in `StripeSubscriptionSection`'s description, and the ad credit is applied OUTSIDE Stripe by the Meta ads integration. There is no month-1 discount Price, Coupon, or column. **Trigger to revisit:** if finance wants the month-1 split to actually appear on the Stripe invoice, that needs a one-off тВм99 Price + a тВм200 negative-amount line or a Coupon тАФ a real model change. **Follow-up (dynamic plan info):** the displayed PRICE is no longer hardcoded тАФ `usePlanInfo()` resolves name/amount/currency/interval live from the Stripe Price object (`lib/integrations/stripe/plan-info.ts`, 5-min cache). The тВм99/тВм200 month-1 sentence is the ONE remaining hardcoded plan figure тАФ it is sanctioned marketing prose (Stripe never had тВм99 or тВм200, so it cannot drift *from Stripe*), but it assumes a тВм299 total: if the Stripe Price ever changes, that sentence needs a manual copy edit. Move it to a Stripe Price `metadata` key if it should become dynamic too. (2) **Webhook events are applied idempotently but NOT ordering-aware.** Each `customer.subscription.*` event carries the full subscription object, so applying any one gives correct state тАФ but a delayed/out-of-order older `.updated` arriving after a newer one would write stale state. No event-dedup table, no `created`-timestamp compare. **Trigger:** if operators report a status flickering or going stale, add an event-sequence guard. (3) **The payment-failed alert emails every admin-role user**, not operators scoped to that client's `accessible_client_ids` тАФ fine for the single-operator V1; revisit when junior-operator scoping matters. (4) **The Resend send in `notify.ts` is a minimal inline send**, not the full Resend integration (a later session) тАФ when `RESEND_API_KEY` is unset the alert job records `skipped` and the operator sees nothing. (5) **`client_stripe_customers` has no `tests/rls/` coverage** тАФ this session added columns to it but no new table and no new policy (the existing operator-SELECT / service-role-write policy is column-agnostic), so the "new RLS resource тЖТ new RLS test" rule above is not triggered. The pre-existing gap (the table got no RLS test when migration `0052` created it) should be closed in a future RLS-harness pass тАФ it is operator-only + service-role-write, low risk. (6) **Pricing is env config** (`STRIPE_PRICE_ID_STANDARD`), not a `stripe_prices` table тАФ promote to a table when there is more than one tier (migration `0057`'s comment carries the plan).
